name:G‚Äçu‚Äçe‚Äçs‚Äçt‚Äç ‚ÄçU‚Äçs‚Äçe‚Äçr
info:Deluxe Double Room
info:Stayed in January 2023
info:Couples
info:1 Review
rating:5
posted:Posted February 7, 2023
msg:The English-speaking reception staff were very efficient. Due to the lingering cigarette smell in our 'non-smoking' room, they changed our room with little fuss.
The expansive views of the waterways and city lights from our sofa were very pleasant to enjoy with wine and cheese bought from the local Ole (supermarket in MixC that stocks a large range of imported products). 
During our 4-night stay, the Western style buffet breakfast maintained a high standard throughout, offering everything from honey on the comb (for toast), to pastries, freshly cooked pancakes and waffles, traditional bacon-eggs-baked beans-hash browns-grill tomatoes, freshly brewed espresso, and everything in between. Due to our nationality, we did not sample the Chinese buffet breakfast.
The hotel was situated a short walk from the closest subway station and a manageable walk from MixC, an upmarket shopping center with a myriad of restaurants to choose from for dinner. We did not eat at the hotel restaurant for evening meals, so am unable to comment on that.
The room offered a deep bath, which was a treat after each full day of sightseeing around Xiamen Island.
Overall, we enjoyed our stay very much, and will continue to use the hotel brand on future travels.

Considering that we had eaten Fujian cuisine for a few days in Quanzhou, we also wanted to change our taste, but the restaurant told us that there were many people eating Hong Kong-style snacks today, and there was no time to make them at noon, so we ordered directly. We ordered according to the menu, but when we checked out, something unpleasant happened. First, we drank three cups of boiled water, but we were charged 28 per person for tea, without any prior explanation. After asking, the manager said that it was charged because there was no service charge. What is this? Charging tea fees without service fees? No prior explanation, and no tea for us? We didn't care about it because people were working overtime during the Spring Festival, but it was even more infuriating later. Second, we had finished our meal, and the waiter ordered Hong Kong snacks for a father and daughter who had just sat down in the distance. I don't know if this restaurant is bullying out-of-town tourists or the "eating style" is too ugly. Anyway, we will not go there again. I advise all out-of-town tourists not to go there, beware of being ripped off! In addition, the hotel is indeed a bit old, and the TV is too small.

msg:Overall, it's ok, and the price/performance ratio is quite high.
Location: Frankly speaking, the location is a bit awkward. You have to walk between the two remaining rail transits. If there is a car, ignore it. I always call for a car when I come in or out. There is nothing within a 10-minute walk, and the surrounding area is a construction site.
Check-in: The room was reserved in advance and met my reservation preferences. Registration was also relatively smooth and check-in was normal.
Room: I booked a luxury suite. Other netizens said they could see the lake view, but when I looked out, it was all roads and construction sites. After my later research, it may not be accurate. The naming rules of this hotel's rooms are: deluxe √ó room is on the low floor, exclusive deluxe √ó room is on the high floor, and executive √ó room is on the executive floor. The exclusive deluxe suite I booked is a suite on a high floor. All suite bookings include lounge access. The decoration of the room is a bit old, and traces of history can be seen. The suite contains 2 bathrooms. The toilet in the master bathroom is a later-modified smart toilet, and the toiletries are from L'Occitane. Upon check-in, we were given a bottle of sparkling wine, a pack of marshmallows, a box of macarons, a piece of Chris**as cake, and a fruit plate. The guest guide in the room said that those who book a suite should have a daily fruit plate. , only the fruit plate is provided for the first stay. In the room minibar, only Coke, sugar-free Coke, Sprite, and Chinese herbal tea are free, and the rest are charged. The tea bags come in four bags, but there are actually only three bags. There is a capsule coffee machine. The curtains are electric. The bathroom remote control is broken. I think the pillows are a bit firm and high.
Meal: I ate breakfast on the second floor. There were quite a lot of people. I think the food was quite rich, including all the usual food. Fish ball soup and sand tea noodles are Xiamen snack features. Afternoon tea, I had it in the lounge, including fruits, cakes, sandwiches, soft drinks and coffee. Happy hour in the lounge in the evening, 17:00-21:00, maybe because of the New Year's Day, there is a rhythm that obviously cannot be kept up with. The plates are empty, the replenishment is not timely, and there is sashimi during the happy hour.
Spa and fitness: I visited the gym and it was normal. Just look at the pictures. The pictures are everything. There are two spas. The one on the 5th floor is the hotel's own. Hotel guests can enjoy a 15% discount after adding 6% to the price list. There is another one on the 6th floor, which is rented out by the hotel.
Generally speaking, it's good, but because the surrounding area is too deserted, if you want to walk around (note that you use walking here) after checking in, there is really nothing to see.
